      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_141860'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/141860.The_Science_Fiction_Hall_of_Fame_Volume_One_1929_1964?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Science Fiction Hall of Fame, Volume One, 1929-1964<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/4338.Robert_Silverberg?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Robert Silverberg<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.34 avg rating &mdash; 5,198 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1970\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer11918104611448264162\">If you own only one anthology of classic science fiction, it should be The Science Fiction Hall of Fame: Volume One, 1929-1964. Selected by a vote of the membership of the Science Fiction Writers of America (SFWA), these 26 reprints represent the bes<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText11918104611448264162\" style=\"display:none\">If you own only one anthology of classic science fiction, it should be The Science Fiction Hall of Fame: Volume One, 1929-1964. Selected by a vote of the membership of the Science Fiction Writers of America (SFWA), these 26 reprints represent the best, most important, and most influential stories and authors in the field. The contributors are a Who\'s Who of classic SF, with every Golden Age giant included: Isaac Asimov, Ray Bradbury, Arthur C. Clarke, John W. Campbell, Robert A. Heinlein, Fritz Leiber, Cordwainer Smith, Theodore Sturgeon, and Roger Zelazny. Other contributors are less well known outside the core SF readership. Three of the contributors are famous for one story--but what stories!--Tom Godwin\'s pivotal hard-SF tale, &quot;The Cold Equations&quot;; Jerome Bixby\'s &quot;It\'s a Good Life&quot; (made only more infamous by the chilling Twilight Zone adaptation); and Daniel Keyes\'s &quot;Flowers for Algernon&quot; (brought to mainstream fame by the movie adaptation, Charly). The collection has some minor but frustrating flaws. There are no contributor biographies, which is bad enough when the author is a giant; but it\'s especially sad for contributors who have become unjustly obscure. Each story\'s original publication date is in small print at the bottom of the first page. And neither this fine print nor the copyright page identifies the magazines in which the stories first appeared. Prefaced by editor Robert Silverberg\'s introduction, which describes SFWA and details the selection process, The Science Fiction Hall of Fame: Volume One, 1929-1964 is a wonderful book for the budding SF fan. Experienced SF readers should compare the table of contents to their library before making a purchase decision. Fans who contemplate giving this book to non-SF readers should bear in mind that, while several of the collected stories can measure up to classic mainstream literary stories, the less literarily-acceptable stories are weighted toward the front of the collection; adult mainstream-literature fans may not get very far into The Science Fiction Hall of Fame: Volume One, 1929-1964. --Cynthia Ward\n\n· Introduction · Robert Silverberg · in \n· A Martian Odyssey [Tweel] · Stanley G. When famous adventurer Sir Richard Francis Burton dies, the last thing he expects to do is awaken naked on a foreign planet along the shores of a seemingly endless river. But that\'s where Burton and billions of other humans (plus a few nonhumans) find themselves as the epic Riverworld saga begins. It seems that all of Earthly humanity has been resurrected on the planet, each with an indestructible container that provides three meals a day, cigarettes, alcoholic beverages, a lighter, and the odd tube of lipstick. But why? And by whom? That\'s what Burton and a handful of fellow adventurers are determined to discover as they construct a boat and set out in search of the river\'s source, thought to be millions of miles away. Although there are many hardships during the journey--including an encounter with the infamous Hermann Goring--Burton\'s resolve to complete his quest is strengthened by a visit from the Mysterious Stranger, a being who claims to be a renegade within the very group that created the Riverworld.           <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/7415.Harlan_Ellison"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1377708311p3/7415.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8908057553598775534">Harlan Jay Ellison was a prolific American writer of short stories, novellas, teleplays, essays, and criticism.<br/><br/>His literary and television work has received many awards. He wrote for the original series of both <i>The Outer Limits</i> and <i>Star Trek</i> as well as <i>The Alfred Hitchcock Hour</i>; edited the multiple-award-winning short story anthology series <i>Dangerous Visions</i>; and served as creative consultant/writ</span>
  <span id="freeText8908057553598775534" style="display:none">Harlan Jay Ellison was a prolific American writer of short stories, novellas, teleplays, essays, and criticism.<br /><br />His literary and television work has received many awards. He wrote for the original series of both <i>The Outer Limits</i> and <i>Star Trek</i> as well as <i>The Alfred Hitchcock Hour</i>; edited the multiple-award-winning short story anthology series <i>Dangerous Visions</i>; and served as creative consultant/writer to the science fiction TV series <i>The New Twilight Zone</i> and <i>Babylon 5</i>.<br /><br />Several of his short fiction pieces have been made into movies, such as the classic "The Boy and His Dog".<br /><br />webmaster@harlanellison.com</span>
